          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3440117552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14590958925914234248"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596802891i/29929269._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖<br/><br/>When I first read the blurb:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929067.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>30% into the book:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929068.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>70% into the book;<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929069.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>80% into the book:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929070.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929071.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>After the book is done:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929072.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929073.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929074.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖<br/><br/>So, I actually don't know what to say. I understood where the author was going with it and I loved the beginning but imo, somewhere in the middle it all went downhill.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929075.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(I just couldn't resist it😂)<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Plot:</u>
</b><br/><br/>Maggie and West meet one Friday night. Maggie doesn't talk. She can, but she doesn't. She saw her own father shoot her mother and since then she stopped. She stopped talki</span>
  <span id="freeText14590958925914234248" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596802891i/29929269._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖<br><br>When I first read the blurb:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929067.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>30% into the book:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929068.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>70% into the book;<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929069.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>80% into the book:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929070.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929071.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After the book is done:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929072.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929073.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929074.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖❖<br><br>So, I actually don't know what to say. I understood where the author was going with it and I loved the beginning but imo, somewhere in the middle it all went downhill.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596799998ra/29929075.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(I just couldn't resist it😂)<br><br><b>
  <u>Plot:</u>
</b><br><br>Maggie and West meet one Friday night. Maggie doesn't talk. She can, but she doesn't. She saw her own father shoot her mother and since then she stopped. She stopped talking, stopped going out, stopped being her. She stopped living all together. West's father is dying of cancer and he has no one to confide in. So, when he see's Maggie that night at a party, he confides in her, thinking that she can't speak. But what he doesn't expect, is the green-eyed beauty, to reply and share her demons which are worse and far more greater than he could've ever imagined. <br><br>He's the only one she talks too and she's the only one who knows about his dad. Through grief and emotions, they form a bond that no one understands but brings both of them the feeling of home, the feeling of belonging. <br><br>Abby Glines did a wonderful job to portray the grief the characters were going through. I really loved how Maggie was there for West <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when his dad passed away <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and how she was <b>always</b> there to comfort him. <br><br>I think things started to go downhill for me from the time when West and Abby turned from "just-friends" to "more-than-friends." Okay, lets be real, they were never "just friends" even when they were, but whatever helps you sleep at night I guess. Anyway, imo West was always one foot out the door since the time they started dating. According to me, Maggie was too conflicted with her feelings and would have appreciated better insight on in. But what bothered me the most was the whole "I'm only your crutch and nothing more" thing, that imo added unnecessary conflict. <br><br>Other than that, according to me, there wasn't a plot really and just two teenagers battling with grief. Or should I say one teenager battling with grief while leaning on the other? Cause we didn't really see Maggie really being sad or anything, except for the fact that she stopped talking, there was nothing. Especially when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she found out her dad had committed suicide <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I expected some reaction. But her? Nothing! <br><br>I still liked the book and liked how the author had portrayed both of our main characters and the way they battled with their demons. Brady was overprotected, and I've seen how many people didn't like that, but I actually really liked it. Brady knew what she had gone through, and even though he wouldn't show it and acted indifferent, he really cared for her and wanted what was best for her and West.<br><br>Overall, I'd rate this book about 3.5 stars (rounded upto 3). If you guys are looking for a light, short book with no OTT drama (except for the ex's, which btw I hated, he kinda liked Maggie but he was still moving around, and I don't like my H's moving around in the books) you should give it a try. I'm not sure if I would really recommend this book, but if the things I didn't like don't bother you, you could give this one a try.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1474886249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1474886249" />
    <a title="Kels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28386116-kels"><img alt="Kels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466351542p2/28386116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1474886249?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kels" href="/user/show/28386116-kels">Kels</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Coho fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=bag-full-of-meh">bag-full-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=na">na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=why-oh-why">why-oh-why</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=its-not-me-its-you">its-not-me-its-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=ok-maybe-its-me-too">ok-maybe-its-me-too</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=blah">blah</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1474886249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3964666345317942966">This was my first Abbi Glines book, and it was such a huge disappointment. I almost feel bad for how much I dislike it, because I'll admit: she has a simplistic charm in her writing that made this an easy, quick read. But as far content goes, I'll pass. <br/><br/>Abbi Glines is certainly a gifted and talented writer. Her words aren't striking, poetic, witty, or powerful, but they are compelling all the same. Her prose has such a fluid and easy flow, slightly reminiscent of Coho's writing style, that doesn</span>
  <span id="freeText3964666345317942966" style="display:none">This was my first Abbi Glines book, and it was such a huge disappointment. I almost feel bad for how much I dislike it, because I'll admit: she has a simplistic charm in her writing that made this an easy, quick read. But as far content goes, I'll pass. <br /><br />Abbi Glines is certainly a gifted and talented writer. Her words aren't striking, poetic, witty, or powerful, but they are compelling all the same. Her prose has such a fluid and easy flow, slightly reminiscent of Coho's writing style, that doesn't put any pressure on the reader to read in between the lines, or take pauses to digest the meaning of her sentences. And you know, every now and then, a light read is just what I need. It's refreshing and freeing. But that's about all I have positive to say about this book.<br /><br />I'm sure if you've picked up a YA or NA book lately, then this one would seem particularly familiar to you. We have our female protagonist, Maggie, who has a traumatic past she's still learning to cope with by voluntarily becoming mute. We have our male protagonist, West, who's a <s>sleazeball</s> <s>womanizer</s> <s>user</s> troubled soul that every girl wants a go at and every girl gets her turn. The two meet and <i>Bada Bing Bada Boom</i> instant <s>lust</s> love. <br /><br />But that doesn't get West to stop getting his share of blow jobs in the high school bathroom... and because he's going through tough time: That's. Okay. <br /><br />Maggie just needs to be there for him. Whenever. Wherever. Whatever... If he needs her to hold his hand while he's getting off with some other random girl, I'm sure she would have been up for it. Because only she can save him and blah blah blah. Seriously, that's not even the worst of it. Because later on, we also have to deal with their blossoming unhealthy, possessive, and controlling relationship. I mean West doesn't even want Maggie to speak to anyone else because that would be... um... a step in the right direction considering she hasn't spoken to anyone besides him in years?? And just when I think Mrs. Abbi Glines gets it, and she's showing us that this isn't what a normal, high school relationship looks like by allowing Maggie to break it off with him, we find out it's because Maggie doesn't think this behavior is okay... well, at least not when West hasn't said that he loves her. Because we all know, those three words make volatile relationships worth staying in. <br /><br />Sigh. I'm so over this book. I'm so over books that portray relationships--especially teenage relationships!! Come on. What message are we sending to our youths here?!--with jealousy, possessiveness, and unhealthy behaviors (that wouldn't be acceptable in adult relationships) all romanticized with rose colored glasses. Yep. I'm over it and I never even hopped on that train to begin with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3964666345317942966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1430055576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430055576" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18085807-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392065462p2/18085807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430055576?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/18085807-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18085807-sabrina?shelf=college-new-adult-romance">college-new-adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18085807-sabrina?shelf=sports-jocks-fighters">sports-jocks-fighters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430055576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7847721093382887498"><b>
  <i>Re-read 7/31/16</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>3.5 'Painful' Stars</b><br/><br/>Maggie moves in with her Aunt and Uncle after a tragic event leads her to being all alone in the world. Their son Brady is her age so her aunt makes him take care of Maggie and take her around with him. Really though, Maggie would rather be alone and not around people that don't understand her. She hasn't talked to anyone since that terrible night and she has no desire to. But then she meets West...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446334137ra/16789983.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>West is going through hell and he's all alone. He doesn't wa</span>
  <span id="freeText7847721093382887498" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Re-read 7/31/16</i>
</b><br><br><b>3.5 'Painful' Stars</b><br><br>Maggie moves in with her Aunt and Uncle after a tragic event leads her to being all alone in the world. Their son Brady is her age so her aunt makes him take care of Maggie and take her around with him. Really though, Maggie would rather be alone and not around people that don't understand her. She hasn't talked to anyone since that terrible night and she has no desire to. But then she meets West...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446334137ra/16789983.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>West is going through hell and he's all alone. He doesn't want the pitying looks or the 'I'm sorry's' when he knows that no one else actually understands what he's going through. But then he meets Maggie, his friends mute cousin, and he know's she's the only one he can talk to. Even is she doesn't talk back. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446334137ra/16789984.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In all honestly, I had never planned on reading this book. I don't really like the high school stories and I had given up on Abbi Glines books after they started to go bad for me. But when I was in a slump and couldn't find anything that interested me I decided to try this and see if something that I normally wouldn't read would help me out of the slump. I'm really glad I gave it a shot and I ended up enjoying the story.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446334137ra/16789985.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>West was such an intense character and my heart broke while reading what he had to go through. I can't say that my emotions were completely affected by the book but I would be lying if I said West didn't make me feel some shit. I like how he was at such a loss with what to do with Maggie and how he felt about her but I knew he would figure it out. He was a really strong character to deal with everything going on his life and not break down every single day. When he finally did break, though, I just wanted to hug him and tell him everything would be okay.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446334137ra/16789986.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Maggie was really interesting and I was so into her story and what happened to her. I actually wish we got to know more about her past because I feel like we were only told the basics and like I was missing things. I liked her with West but by herself I got a little annoyed with her character and that she never stood up for herself. Even though she couldn't talk back to people picking on her I would have liked to see her be a little more strong and not just upset at what the people were saying. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446334137ra/16789987.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bottom line, this was a good story and I'm really glad I was in a bit of a slump that made me give West and Maggie a chance. I will definitely be reading the next story which I hope will be Gunners.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7847721093382887498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hmDcOc6SKYiUHFbjpJSq9ZIPzcG6lgk3xqdFhjx5I9xJLvrOjVPMYJswFYM6JIuYIjUe4LorTNZOGdHg3CLI9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rc422U5cS+38K8LDjm2ZoZe/TNQnm6guGlbQFLy0a6OKgBAuDZ2uBfMHgaMQ3bjMJ4Wf9Scm7c+S6ERyXO+AiQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4973459775902665563">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be Britis</span>
  <span id="freeText4973459775902665563" style="display:none">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be British but alas she was born in Alabama. When asked how many books she has written she has to stop and count on her fingers. When she’s not locked away writing, she is reading, shopping (major shoe and purse addiction), sneaking off to the movies alone, and listening to the drama in her teenagers lives while making mental notes on the good stuff to use later. Don’t judge.<br /><br />You can connect with Abbi online in several different ways. She uses social media to procrastinate.<br /></span>
